GT Equivalence Verification (PO3)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v
Candidate formulas: 69

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,v)=0.106256914230442\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.484396978017638\,\sin(v)\;-\;0.968793956035275\,v.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **(i)** a pure \(\sin(t)\) term with constant amplitude, **(ii)** a pure \(\sin(v)\) term with constant amplitude, **(iii)** a pure linear-in-\(v\) term, and **(iv)** no other unavoidable dependence (no denominators in \(t\), no exponentials in \(t\) or \(v\), no piecewise Max/Abs artifacts unless they can be made to disappear globally).

Below, “can be killed” means we can set a coefficient to 0 (or otherwise choose parameters) so the term vanishes for all \(t,v\).

---

### 1.
Has everything divided by \((c3 v^2+1)\). To match GT (which has no such factor), must set \(c3=0\) so denominator is 1. Then expression becomes a sum of three sine terms: \(\sin(c1+c2 v)\), \(v^2\sin(c5+c6 t)\), \(\sin(c6 t+c8)\). GT needs \(\sin(t)\), \(\sin(v)\), and \(v\) (linear), not \(v^2\) times sine. You can kill the \(v^2\sin(\cdot)\) term by \(c4=0\), but there is still **no linear \(v\)** term available. ❌

### 2.
Contains \(c5 e^{c6 t}\cos(c7 v+c8)\): mixes \(t\) and \(v\) via exponential in \(t\) multiplying a \(v\)-cosine. GT has separate \(\sin(t)\) and \(\sin(v)\) with constant amplitudes. You could set \(c6=0\) to remove the \(t\)-dependence in that amplitude, but then you still have \(\cos(\cdot)\) in \(v\) (convertible to \(\sin\) by phase shift) **and** there is no linear \(v\) term. ❌

### 3.
Form: constant + \(e^{c2 t}\sin(c3 t+c4)\) + \(c5 v + c6 v^3\).
Can set \(c0=0\), \(c2=0\) to remove exponential, choose \(c3=1,c4=0\) to get \(\sin(t)\), set \(c6=0\) to remove \(v^3\), and set \(c5=-0.968793956035275\) to match linear \(v\). But there is **no \(\sin(v)\)** term. ❌

### 4.
Has \(e^{c6\sin(c7 v+c8)}\), which cannot become a linear combination of \(\sin(v)\) and \(v\) globally unless killed (set \(c5=0\)). Then reduces to constant + \(e^{c2 t}\sin(\cdot)\) only; still missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 5.
Includes Max(0,±v) piecewise terms and a \(v(c6+t)^{c7}\) coupling \(t\) and \(v\). To match GT (smooth, not piecewise), must kill Max terms (set their coefficients 0) and kill the mixed power term (set \(c5=0\)). Then only \(\sin(c1 t+c2)\) remains: missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 6.
Has \(c0/(c1+t)\) and cosine-in-\(t\) plus \(v\) and \(v^3\). To match GT, must remove \(1/(c1+t)\) term (set \(c0=0\)) and remove \(v^3\) (set \(c7=0\)). Cosine can be phase-shifted to sine and exponential killed by \(c3=0\). Then we can match \(\sin(t)\) and linear \(v\), but still **no \(\sin(v)\)**. ❌

### 7.
Has \(v e^{c6 v^2}\). To get linear \(v\), need \(c6=0\) so it becomes \(c5 v\). Then it’s constant + \(\sin(t)\)-type term + linear \(v\), but **no \(\sin(v)\)**. ❌

### 8.
Has \(c0/(c1+t)\) (must be killed: \(c0=0\)). Then has \(\sin(c3 v+c4)\) (good for \(\sin(v)\)) and \(e^{c6 t}\cos(c7 t+c8)\) (can become \(\sin(t)\) by setting \(c6=0\) and phase shift). But there is **no linear \(v\)** term. ❌

### 9.
Form: constant + \(e^{c2 t}\sin(c3 t+c4)\) + \(c5\sin(c6 v+c7)\).
This can match \(\sin(t)\) (set \(c2=0,c3=1,c4=0\), \(c1=0.106256914230442\)) and \(\sin(v)\) (set \(c6=1,c7=0\), \(c5=-0.484396978017638\)), and set constant \(c0=0\). But there is **no linear \(v\)** term. ❌

### 10.
Has piecewise Max terms with \(e^{c4|v|}\) and also a \(e^{c7 t^2}\sin(c8 v+c9)\) term. To match smooth GT, would need to kill the Max terms (set coefficients 0) and kill the \(t^2\)-exponential term (set \(c6=0\)). Then only \(\sin(t)\) remains. Missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 11.
Contains \(c0/(c1+t)\) (kill with \(c0=0\)), plus \(e^{c3 v}\sin(c4 t+c5)\) which couples \(v\) into amplitude of \(\sin(t)\) unless \(c3=0\). Then second term becomes pure \(\sin(t)\). Third term is \(v e^{c7 t}\sin(c8+c9 v^2)\) which is not linear \(v\) unless killed (set \(c6=0\)). Then no \(\sin(v)\) and no linear \(v\). ❌

### 12.
All terms divided by \((c3 v^2+1)\). To remove denominator, set \(c3=0\). Then terms are \(c0 v^2\sin(c1+c2 t)+c4\sin(c2 t+c5)+c6 v\). We can match \(\sin(t)\) via the \(c4\) term (choose \(c2=1\), phase), and match linear \(v\) via \(c6 v\). But there is **no \(\sin(v)\)** term. ❌

### 13.
Only \(\sin(t)\) plus piecewise Max/exp(v^2) terms. To avoid piecewise behavior, must kill those terms, leaving only \(\sin(t)\). Missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 14.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(v^5\) + piecewise exp(v^2) Max terms. Must kill \(v^5\) and Max terms to avoid extra dependence; then only \(\sin(t)\). Missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 15.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(v^{c4}\) + piecewise terms. Even if set \(c3=0\) and kill piecewise terms, no \(\sin(v)\) and no linear \(v\) unless you try \(v^{c4}\) with \(c4=1\). But then you get linear \(v\) yes; still no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 16.
Constant + \(\sin(t)\) + \(e^{c5\sin(c6+c7 v)}\). To match GT, must kill the exponential-sine term (set \(c4=0\)), leaving constant + \(\sin(t)\). Missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 17.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(e^{c4 v}\) + piecewise terms. Kill \(e^{c4 v}\) (set \(c3=0\)) and kill piecewise terms; left with \(\sin(t)\). Missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 18.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise exp(|v|) Max terms + \(v^3\). Kill piecewise and \(v^3\); left with \(\sin(t)\). Missing \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\). ❌

### 19.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(c3\max(0,-v)+c4\max(0,v)+c5 v^3\). To be globally linear in \(v\), the Max terms would need to combine to \(kv\) for all \(v\), but \(\max(0,v)-\max(0,-v)=v\) is possible only if coefficients are opposite: set \(c4=k, c3=-k\). That yields \(k v\) (good). Also set \(c5=0\). Then we can match \(\sin(t)\) and linear \(v\). Still **no \(\sin(v)\)**. ❌

### 20.
Has piecewise exp(v^2) Max terms and rational-in-\(t\) terms \(v/(c6 t+c7)\), \(1/(c6 t+c7)\). GT has no such \(t\)-denominators; must kill them (set \(c5=0,c8=0\)) and kill piecewise terms. Left with \(\sin(t)\) only. ❌

### 21.
Has \(c0/(c1+t)\) (must kill: \(c0=0\)), plus \(c2 v^3 + c3 v + c4\cos(c5 t+c6)\). Can match \(\sin(t)\) via cosine phase shift and match linear \(v\) via \(c3\), set \(c2=0\). Still **no \(\sin(v)\)**. ❌

### 22.
Same as 21 but sine in \(t\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 23.
Constant + \(\sin(t)\) + \(c4 v + c5 v^3\). Can match \(\sin(t)\) and linear \(v\) (set \(c5=0\)), but no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 24.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(\sin(c4 v+c5)\) + \(v|v|\). Kill \(v|v|\) (set \(c6=0\)). Then can match \(\sin(t)\) and \(\sin(v)\) by choosing frequencies/phases and amplitudes. Still **no linear \(v\)** term. ❌

### 25.
\(\sin(c1+c2 v) + \cos(c4 t+c5)\). Can match \(\sin(v)\) and \(\sin(t)\) (cos phase shift), but no linear \(v\). ❌

### 26.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(\sin(v)\). Missing linear \(v\). ❌

### 27.
\(\sin(t) + t^{c4}\sin(v)\). To get pure \(\sin(v)\) with constant amplitude, need \(t^{c4}\) constant: set \(c4=0\) so \(t^0=1\). Then we have \(\sin(t)+\sin(v)\), still missing linear \(v\). ❌

### 28.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise terms + \(t(c6+v)^{c7}\) mixing \(t\) and \(v\). Must kill mixed term and piecewise terms; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 29.
Constant + \(\sin(t)\) + \(v e^{c5 v^2}\). Set \(c5=0\) to get linear \(v\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 30.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise terms + \(v\log(c7 v^2+1)\). Kill piecewise and log term to avoid mismatch; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 31.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(\log(c4 v+1)\) + piecewise terms. Log can’t become \(\sin(v)\) or linear \(v\) globally; must kill it and piecewise terms; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 32.
Only \(\sin(t)\) plus piecewise exp terms. Kill piecewise terms; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 33.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(v^3\log(\cdot)\) + piecewise + \(v\log(\cdot)\). No way to turn logs into \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\) simultaneously; must kill them and piecewise; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 34.
Constant + \(\sin(t)\) + \(\cos(v)\). Can match \(\sin(v)\) via phase shift, but no linear \(v\). ❌

### 35.
Constant + \(\sin(t)\) + \(\sin(v)\). Missing linear \(v\). ❌

### 36.
Has \(c0/(c1+t)\) (kill with \(c0=0\)), plus \(\sin(t)\), plus \(\sin(v)/(c8 v^2+1)\). To match pure \(\sin(v)\), need \(c8=0\). Then we have \(\sin(t)+\sin(v)\). Still no linear \(v\). ❌

### 37.
Has \(c0/(c1+t)\) (kill), plus \(\sin(t)\), plus \(v/(c6 v^2+1)\). To get linear \(v\), need \(c6=0\). Then we can match \(\sin(t)\) and linear \(v\), but no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 38.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(\log(c4 t+1)\) + piecewise terms. Must kill log and piecewise; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 39.

### 41.

### 42.

### 43.
Has \(c0/(c1+t)\) and a sigmoid-like \(c3/(c4 e^{c5 v}+1)\) plus \(\sin(t)\). Cannot become \(-\sin(v)-v\) globally; killing those leaves only \(\sin(t)\) and constant. ❌

### 44.
\(\sin(t) + v^{c4} + v|v| + v/(c7+|v|)\). Absolute values prevent global equivalence to a smooth linear+sin unless those terms are killed. If kill them all, only \(\sin(t)\). If keep \(v^{c4}\) with \(c4=1\) to get linear \(v\), still no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 46.
\(\sin(t) + c3 v +\) piecewise exp(|v|) Max terms \(+\;c7 v^3\). Kill piecewise terms and \(v^3\). Then can match \(\sin(t)\) and linear \(v\), but no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 47.
\(\sin(t)\) plus rational-in-\(t\) terms \(t/(c4 t+c5)\), \(1/(c4 t+c5)\) and piecewise terms. Must kill rational terms and piecewise terms; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 48.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(c3 v\sin(c4+c5 v^2)\). Second term is not a sum of linear \(v\) and \(\sin(v)\); to remove it set \(c3=0\), leaving only \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 49.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise exp(|v|) Max terms + \(c6 v + c7 v|v|\). Kill piecewise and \(v|v|\). Then can match \(\sin(t)\) and linear \(v\), but no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 50.
\(\sin(t) + c3 v^3 + c4 v|v| + c5 v\). Kill \(v^3\) and \(v|v|\). Then \(\sin(t)+\)linear \(v\). No \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 51.
\(c0 v^3 + c1 v + c2\cos(c3 t+c4)\). Can match \(\sin(t)\) (phase shift), linear \(v\) (set \(c1\)), kill \(v^3\) (set \(c0=0\)). No \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 52.
\(\sin(t) + c3 v^3 + c4 v\). Kill \(v^3\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 53.

### 54.

### 55.

### 56.
\(\sin(t)\) + \(\sin(t)\) (another sine) + piecewise terms. Even if combine sines into one \(\sin(t)\) and kill piecewise, still no \(\sin(v)\) and no linear \(v\). ❌

### 57.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise terms + \(\log(c7 v^2+1)\cos(\text{t})\). Log term couples \(t\) and \(v\); must kill it and piecewise; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 58.
\(\sin(t) + v|v| + v/(c5+|v|) + v^3\). Abs prevents global match; killing nonlinear terms leaves only \(\sin(t)\). No \(\sin(v)\) and linear \(v\) not present unless you keep \(v/(c5+|v|)\) which is not linear. ❌

### 59.
\(\sin(t) + v^3 e^{c4 t} +\) piecewise + \(v e^{c4 t}\). To get linear \(v\) independent of \(t\), need \(c4=0\) and kill \(v^3\) and piecewise. Then \(\sin(t)+\)linear \(v\). No \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 60.
\(\sin(t) + v|v| + v/(c5+|v|) + v^{c7}\log(c8|v|+1)\). Not reducible to \(\sin(v)+v\) globally; killing terms leaves \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 61.
\(\sin(t) + v|v| + v/(c5+|v|) + c6 v + c7 v^3\). Kill abs-based and \(v^3\) terms; then \(\sin(t)+\)linear \(v\). No \(\sin(v)\). ❌

### 62.

### 63.

### 64.
\(\sin(t)\) + terms involving \(\max(0,\pm v)/(c4+\max(0,-v)+\max(0,v))\) and piecewise exp terms. Those are inherently piecewise in \(v\) unless killed. Killing them leaves \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 65.
Constant + \(e^{c2 t}\sin(\cdot)\) + \(\sin(t)\sin(v)\) product. Product term cannot appear in GT; must kill it (set \(c5=0\)). Then no \(\sin(v)\) and no linear \(v\). ❌

### 66.

### 67.
\(\sin(t) + t^{c4} +\) piecewise terms. Must kill \(t^{c4}\) (set \(c3=0\)) and piecewise; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 68.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise terms + \(e^{c7 v^2}\sin(t)\) coupling. Must kill coupling and piecewise; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

### 69.
\(\sin(t)\) + piecewise terms + \(e^{c7 t}\sin(t)\) extra time-dependent amplitude. Must kill extra term and piecewise; left with \(\sin(t)\). ❌

---

No candidate can simultaneously produce **all three required components** \(\sin(t)\), \(\sin(v)\), and linear \(v\) without introducing forbidden extra structure (denominators, exponentials, products, or piecewise/abs artifacts), because:
- candidates that can do \(\sin(t)+\sin(v)\) lack linear \(v\),
- candidates that can do \(\sin(t)+v\) lack \(\sin(v)\),
- none provide \(\sin(t)\), \(\sin(v)\), and \(v\) together as an additive separable sum.

Conclusion: No match

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT: 0.106257*sin(t) - 0.484397*sin(v) - 0.968794*v**

This has three terms: a sin(t) term, a sin(v) term, and a linear v term.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Key basis functions in GT:
1. sin(t) — sinusoidal in t with frequency 1
2. sin(v) — sinusoidal in v with frequency 1
3. v — linear in v

No constant offset, no exponentials, no polynomials beyond linear in v, no Max/Abs terms, no 1/t terms, no exp(t) terms.

**Candidate 1:** `c0*sin(c1+c2*v)/(c3*v²+1) + c4*v²*sin(c5+c6*t)/(c3*v²+1) + c7*sin(c6*t+c8)/(c3*v²+1)`

This has all terms divided by (c3*v²+1). If c3=0, denominator=1, giving: c0*sin(c1+c2*v) + c4*v²*sin(c5+c6*t) + c7*sin(c6*t+c8). Set c4=0 to kill v²*sin term. Then: c0*sin(c1+c2*v) + c7*sin(c6*t+c8). This gives sin(v) + sin(t) but no linear v term. **Cannot produce linear v.**
